# Platform Knowledge: Flink Windowing API Extension Points

## Your Task

Map the extension points in Apache Flink's windowing API that a developer would need to implement a custom window assigner. Find: 1. The abstract base class `WindowAssigner` in `flink-streaming-java/src/main/java/org/apache/flink/streaming/api/windowing/assigners/` — report its abstract methods. 2. The `MergingWindowAssigner` subclass that adds `mergeWindows()` for session-style windows. 3. The `Trigger` base class in the triggers package — report the lifecycle methods (`onElement`, `onEventTime`, `onProcessingTime`, `onMerge`). 4. An existing reference implementation: `EventTimeSessionWindows` — report how it implements `assignWindows()` and `mergeWindows()`. 5. The `TimeWindow` class that concrete assigners produce. For each, report the file path, class name, and key method signatures.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the platform domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kafka--0753c489, sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc, sg-evals/camel--1006f047.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/kafka--0753c489` (apache/kafka)
- `sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc` (apache/flink)
- `sg-evals/camel--1006f047` (apache/camel)

28-assistanttext-
Done! I've created `/workspace/answer.json` with a comprehensive mapping of Apache Flink's windowing API extension points. Here's what I found:

## Summary of Findings

**1. WindowAssigner** (base class)
- Abstract methods: `assignWindows()`, `getDefaultTrigger()`, `getWindowSerializer()`, `isEventTime()`

**2. MergingWindowAssigner** (for session-style windows)
- Extends WindowAssigner
- Abstract method: `mergeWindows(Collection<W> windows, MergeCallback<W> callback)`

**3. Trigger** (lifecycle methods)
- Abstract methods: `onElement()`, `onEventTime()`, `onProcessingTime()`, `clear()`
- Non-abstract methods: `canMerge()`, `onMerge()` (with default UnsupportedOperationException)

**4. EventTimeSessionWindows** (reference implementation)
- `assignWindows()`: Creates TimeWindow from timestamp to timestamp + sessionTimeout
- `mergeWindows()`: Delegates to TimeWindow.mergeWindows() static utility

**5. TimeWindow** (concrete window type)
- Constructor: `TimeWindow(long start, long end)`
- Key methods: `getStart()`, `getEnd()`, `maxTimestamp()`, `intersects()`, `cover()`
- Static utility: `mergeWindows()` for merging overlapping windows

All files and method signatures are documented in the answer.json file with their complete locations in the codebase.

\"mergeWindows\"\n    }\n  ],\n  \"text\": \"## Flink Windowing API Extension Points\\n\\nThe Apache Flink windowing API provides extension points through abstract base classes and interfaces that developers must implement to create custom window assigners and triggers.\\n\\n### 1. WindowAssigner (sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc:flink-runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/flink/streaming/api/windowing/assigners/WindowAssigner.java)\\n\\nThe abstract base class `WindowAssigner<T, W extends Window>` is the primary extension point for implementing custom window assignment logic. Developers must implement the following abstract methods:\\n\\n- **`Collection<W> assignWindows(T element, long timestamp, WindowAssignerContext context)`** (line 53): Assigns zero or more windows to an incoming element based on its timestamp and current processing time. The context allows querying the current processing time.\\n\\n- **`Trigger<T, W> getDefaultTrigger()`** (line 65): Returns the default trigger associated with this window assigner. Every window assigner must provide a trigger that determines when window results should be emitted.\\n\\n- **`TypeSerializer<W> getWindowSerializer(ExecutionConfig executionConfig)`** (line 71): Returns a TypeSerializer for the window type produced by this assigner, enabling proper serialization of window metadata.\\n\\n- **`boolean isEventTime()`** (line 77): Indicates whether windows are assigned based on event-time (true) or processing-time (false). This determines how the runtime handles watermarks and timers.\\n\\nAdditionally, the class defines a nested `WindowAssignerContext` interface (line 88) that provides a `getCurrentProcessingTime()` method for the assigner to query system time during window assignment.\\n\\n### 2. MergingWindowAssigner (sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc:flink-runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/flink/streaming/api/windowing/assigners/MergingWindowAssigner.java)\\n\\nThe `MergingWindowAssigner<T, W extends Window>` extends `WindowAssigner` and is used for window types that can overlap and merge (such as session windows). It adds one critical abstract method:\\n\\n- **`void mergeWindows(Collection<W> windows, MergeCallback<W> callback)`** (line 42): Determines which windows (if any) should be merged. When windows need to be merged, the implementation invokes the callback's `merge(Collection<W> toBeMerged, W mergeResult)` method to signal the merge operation.\\n\\nThe class also defines the `MergeCallback<W>` interface (line 49-57) with a single method: `void merge(Collection<W> toBeMerged, W mergeResult)` that implementers call to specify which windows should be merged and what the resulting window should be.\\n\\n### 3. Trigger (sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc:flink-runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/flink/streaming/api/windowing/triggers/Trigger.java)\\n\\nThe abstract base class `Trigger<T, W extends Window>` defines the lifecycle methods for window evaluation. Developers must implement these abstract methods:\\n\\n- **`TriggerResult onElement(T element, long timestamp, W window, TriggerContext ctx)`** (line 67): Called for every element added to a pane. The trigger determines whether the pane should fire and produce results.\\n\\n- **`TriggerResult onProcessingTime(long time, W window, TriggerContext ctx)`** (line 77): Called when a processing-time timer (registered via TriggerContext) fires. Enables triggers to react to system clock progression.\\n\\n- **`TriggerResult onEventTime(long time, W window, TriggerContext ctx)`** (line 87): Called when an event-time timer fires (when watermarks pass a registered time). Enables event-time based trigger logic.\\n\\n- **`void clear(W window, TriggerContext ctx)`** (line 118): Called when a window is being purged. Implementers must clean up any state and delete registered timers.\\n\\nAdditionally, there are non-abstract methods:\\n\\n- **`boolean canMerge()`** (line 97): Returns false by default. Subclasses that support merging should override this to return true.\\n\\n- **`void onMerge(W window, OnMergeContext ctx)`** (line 108): Called when windows merge. The default implementation throws UnsupportedOperationException; merging triggers must override this.\\n\\nThe Trigger class also defines two context interfaces:\\n- **`TriggerContext`** (line 126): Provides methods to register/delete timers, get processing time/watermark, and access partitioned state.\\n- **`OnMergeContext`** (line 189): Extends TriggerContext and adds `mergePartitionedState()` for merging trigger state across merged windows.\\n\\n### 4. EventTimeSessionWindows (sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc:flink-streaming-java/src/main/java/org/apache/flink/streaming/api/windowing/assigners/EventTimeSessionWindows.java)\\n\\nThis concrete reference implementation extends `MergingWindowAssigner<Object, TimeWindow>` and demonstrates how to implement a session-based window assigner:\\n\\n- **`Collection<TimeWindow> assignWindows(Object element, long timestamp, WindowAssignerContext context)`** (line 61-63): Creates a single TimeWindow spanning from the element's timestamp to `timestamp + sessionTimeout`. Each new element starts a new session that can later merge with others if gaps are bridged.\\n\\n- **`void mergeWindows(Collection<TimeWindow> windows, MergeCallback<TimeWindow> c)`** (line 113-115): Delegates to the static utility method `TimeWindow.mergeWindows()`, which handles the logic of identifying overlapping windows and merging them into larger contiguous time windows.\\n\\nThe implementation also provides:\\n- `getDefaultTrigger()`: Returns an EventTimeTrigger to fire windows when event-time advances via watermarks\\n- `getWindowSerializer()`: Returns a TimeWindow.Serializer for proper window serialization\\n- `isEventTime()`: Returns true since session windows are based on element timestamps (event-time)\\n\\nThe class supports both static gap creation via `withGap(Duration)` (line 83) and dynamic gaps via `withDynamicGap()` (line 96) for extracting session timeouts from elements.\\n\\n### 5. TimeWindow (sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc:flink-runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/flink/streaming/api/windowing/windows/TimeWindow.java)\\n\\nThe `TimeWindow` class (extending `Window`) represents a time-based window interval from start (inclusive) to end (exclusive). Key characteristics:\\n\\n- **Constructor**: `TimeWindow(long start, long end)` (line 50): Creates a window representing the time interval [start, end).\\n\\n- **Key accessor methods**:\\n  - `getStart()` (line 61): Returns the inclusive start timestamp\\n  - `getEnd()` (line 71): Returns the exclusive end timestamp\\n  - `maxTimestamp()` (line 84): Returns `end - 1`, the largest timestamp in the window\\n\\n- **Merge utility methods**:\\n  - `intersects(TimeWindow other)` (line 116): Checks if windows overlap or are adjacent\\n  - `cover(TimeWindow other)` (line 121): Creates the minimal window covering both windows\\n  - **`static void mergeWindows(Collection<TimeWindow> windows, MergeCallback<TimeWindow> c)`** (line 208-254): Sorts windows by start time and merges overlapping windows, invoking the callback for each merge group. This is the utility method used by EventTimeSessionWindows and other merging assigners.\\n\\n- **Serialization**: Includes a nested `Serializer` class (line 130) and `TimeWindowSerializerSnapshot` (line 191) for type evolution support.\\n\\n## Summary\\n\\nThe extension points form a chain: WindowAssigner implementations define `assignWindows()` to produce Window instances, specify a Trigger via `getDefaultTrigger()`, and declare whether they support merging (MergingWindowAssigner). Trigger implementations react to element arrivals and timer fires via `onElement()`, `onEventTime()`, and `onProcessingTime()`. For merging scenarios (e.g., session windows), both the assigner implements `mergeWindows()` and the trigger implements `onMerge()` to coordinate window and state consolidation. TimeWindow is the concrete window type produced by most time-based assigners and provides merge utility logic.\\n\"\n}\n",
